{"type":"user","message":{"role":"user","content":[{"tool_use_id":"toolu_015cy5SDEgYEgzHXt88PmFS3","type":"tool_result","content":"{\"content\":\"1: syntax = \\\"proto3\\\";\\n2: \\n3: package envoy.extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3;\\n4: \\n5: import \\\"envoy/config/common/mutation_rules/v3/mutation_rules.proto\\\";\\n6: import \\\"envoy/config/core/v3/base.proto\\\";\\n7: import \\\"envoy/config/core/v3/grpc_service.proto\\\";\\n8: import \\\"envoy/extensions/filters/http/ext_proc/v3/processing_mode.proto\\\";\\n9: import \\\"envoy/type/matcher/v3/string.proto\\\";\\n10: \\n11: import \\\"google/protobuf/duration.proto\\\";\\n12: import \\\"google/protobuf/struct.proto\\\";\\n13: \\n14: import \\\"udpa/annotations/status.proto\\\";\\n15: import \\\"validate/validate.proto\\\";\\n16: \\n17: option java_package = \\\"io.envoyproxy.envoy.extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3\\\";\\n18: option java_outer_classname = \\\"ExtProcProto\\\";\\n19: option java_multiple_files = true;\\n20: option go_package = \\\"github.com/envoyproxy/go-control-plane/envoy/extensions/filters/http/ext_proc/v3;ext_procv3\\\";\\n21: option (udpa.annotations.file_status).package_version_status = ACTIVE;\\n22: \\n23: // [#protodoc-title: External Processing Filter]\\n24: // External Processing Filter\\n25: // [#extension: envoy.filters.http.ext_proc]\\n26: \\n27: // The External Processing filter allows an external service to act on HTTP traffic in a flexible way.\\n28: \\n29: // **Current Implementation Status:**\\n30: // All options and processing modes are implemented except for the following:\\n31: //\\n32: // * \\\"async mode\\\" is not implemented.\\n33: \\n34: // The filter communicates with an external gRPC service called an \\\"external processor\\\"\\n35: // that can do a variety of things with the request and response:\\n36: //\\n37: // * Access and modify the HTTP headers on the request, response, or both\\n38: // * Access and modify the HTTP request and response bodies\\n39: // * Access and modify the dynamic stream metadata\\n40: // * Immediately send an HTTP response downstream and terminate other processing\\n41: //\\n42: // The filter communicates with the server using a gRPC bidirectional stream. After the initial\\n43: // request, the external server is in control over what additional data is sent to it\\n44: // and how it should be processed.\\n45: //\\n46: // By implementing the protocol specified by the stream, the external server can choose:\\n47: //\\n48: // * Whether it receives the response message at all\\n49: // * Whether it receives the message body at all, in separate chunks, or as a single buffer\\n50: // * Whether subsequent HTTP requests are transmitted synchronously or whether they are\\n51: //   sent asynchronously.\\n52: // * To modify request or response trailers if they already exist\\n53: //\\n54: // The filter supports up to six different processing steps. Each is represented by\\n55: // a gRPC stream message that is sent to the external processor. For each message, the\\n56: // processor must send a matching response.\\n57: //\\n58: // * Request headers: Contains the headers from the original HTTP request.\\n59: // * Request body: Delivered if they are present and sent in a single message if\\n60: //   the BUFFERED or BUFFERED_PARTIAL mode is chosen, in multiple messages if the\\n61: //   STREAMED mode is chosen, and not at all otherwise.\\n62: // * Request trailers: Delivered if they are present and if the trailer mode is set\\n63: //   to SEND.\\n64: // * Response headers: Contains the headers from the HTTP response. Keep in mind\\n65: //   that if the upstream system sends them before processing the request body that\\n66: //   this message may arrive before the complete body.\\n67: // * Response body: Sent according to the processing mode like the request body.\\n68: // * Response trailers: Delivered according to the processing mode like the\\n69: //   request trailers.\\n70: //\\n71: // By default, the processor sends only the request and response headers messages.\\n72: // This may be changed to include any of the six steps by changing the processing_mode\\n73: // setting of the filter configuration, or by setting the mode_override of any response\\n74: // from the external processor. The latter is only enabled if allow_mode_override is\\n75: // set to true. This way, a processor may, for example, use information\\n76: // in the request header to determine whether the message body must be examined, or whether\\n77: // the proxy should simply stream it straight through.\\n78: //\\n79: // All of this together allows a server to process the filter traffic in fairly\\n80: // sophisticated ways. For example:\\n81: //\\n82: // * A server may choose to examine all or part of the HTTP message bodies depending\\n83: //   on the content of the headers.\\n84: // * A server may choose to immediately reject some messages based on their HTTP\\n85: //   headers (or other dynamic metadata) and more carefully examine others.\\n86: // * A server may asynchronously monitor traffic coming through the filter by inspecting\\n87: //   headers, bodies, or both, and then decide to switch to a synchronous processing\\n88: //   mode, either permanently or temporarily.\\n89: //\\n90: // The protocol itself is based on a bidirectional gRPC stream. Envoy will send the\\n91: // server\\n92: // :ref:`ProcessingRequest <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingRequest>`\\n93: // messages, and the server must reply with\\n94: // :ref:`ProcessingResponse <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingResponse>`.\\n95: //\\n96: // Stats about each gRPC call are recorded in a :ref:`dynamic filter state\\n97: // <arch_overview_advanced_filter_state_sharing>` object in a namespace matching the filter\\n98: // name.\\n99: //\\n100: // [#next-free-field: 18]\\n101: message ExternalProcessor {\\n102:   reserved 4;\\n103: \\n104:   reserved \\\"async_mode\\\";\\n105: \\n106:   // Configuration for the gRPC service that the filter will communicate with.\\n107:   // The filter supports both the \\\"Envoy\\\" and \\\"Google\\\" gRPC clients.\\n108:   config.core.v3.GrpcService grpc_service = 1 [(validate.rules).message = {required: true}];\\n109: \\n110:   // By default, if the gRPC stream cannot be established, or if it is closed\\n111:   // prematurely with an error, the filter will fail. Specifically, if the\\n112:   // response headers have not yet been delivered, then it will return a 500\\n113:   // error downstream. If they have been delivered, then instead the HTTP stream to the\\n114:   // downstream client will be reset.\\n115:   // With this parameter set to true, however, then if the gRPC stream is prematurely closed\\n116:   // or could not be opened, processing continues without error.\\n117:   bool failure_mode_allow = 2;\\n118: \\n119:   // Specifies default options for how HTTP headers, trailers, and bodies are\\n120:   // sent. See ProcessingMode for details.\\n121:   ProcessingMode processing_mode = 3;\\n122: \\n123:   // Envoy provides a number of :ref:`attributes <arch_overview_attributes>`\\n124:   // for expressive policies. Each attribute name provided in this field will be\\n125:   // matched against that list and populated in the request_headers message.\\n126:   // See the :ref:`attribute documentation <arch_overview_request_attributes>`\\n127:   // for the list of supported attributes and their types.\\n128:   repeated string request_attributes = 5;\\n129: \\n130:   // Envoy provides a number of :ref:`attributes <arch_overview_attributes>`\\n131:   // for expressive policies. Each attribute name provided in this field will be\\n132:   // matched against that list and populated in the response_headers message.\\n133:   // See the :ref:`attribute documentation <arch_overview_attributes>`\\n134:   // for the list of supported attributes and their types.\\n135:   repeated string response_attributes = 6;\\n136: \\n137:   // Specifies the timeout for each individual message sent on the stream and\\n138:   // when the filter is running in synchronous mode. Whenever the proxy sends\\n139:   // a message on the stream that requires a response, it will reset this timer,\\n140:   // and will stop processing and return an error (subject to the processing mode)\\n141:   // if the timer expires before a matching response is received. There is no\\n142:   // timeout when the filter is running in asynchronous mode. Zero is a valid\\n143:   // config which means the timer will be triggered immediately. If not\\n144:   // configured, default is 200 milliseconds.\\n145:   google.protobuf.Duration message_timeout = 7 [(validate.rules).duration = {\\n146:     lte {seconds: 3600}\\n147:     gte {}\\n148:   }];\\n149: \\n150:   // Optional additional prefix to use when emitting statistics. This allows to distinguish\\n151:   // emitted statistics between configured *ext_proc* filters in an HTTP filter chain.\\n152:   string stat_prefix = 8;\\n153: \\n154:   // Rules that determine what modifications an external processing server may\\n155:   // make to message headers. If not set, all headers may be modified except\\n156:   // for \\\"host\\\", \\\":authority\\\", \\\":scheme\\\", \\\":method\\\", and headers that start\\n157:   // with the header prefix set via\\n158:   // :ref:`header_prefix <envoy_v3_api_field_config.bootstrap.v3.Bootstrap.header_prefix>`\\n159:   // (which is usually \\\"x-envoy\\\").\\n160:   // Note that changing headers such as \\\"host\\\" or \\\":authority\\\" may not in itself\\n161:   // change Envoy's routing decision, as routes can be cached. To also force the\\n162:   // route to be recomputed, set the\\n163:   // :ref:`clear_route_cache <envoy_v3_api_field_service.ext_proc.v3.CommonResponse.clear_route_cache>`\\n164:   // field to true in the same response.\\n165:   config.common.mutation_rules.v3.HeaderMutationRules mutation_rules = 9;\\n166: \\n167:   // Specify the upper bound of\\n168:   // :ref:`override_message_timeout <envoy_v3_api_field_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingResponse.override_message_timeout>`\\n169:   // If not specified, by default it is 0, which will effectively disable the ``override_message_timeout`` API.\\n170:   google.protobuf.Duration max_message_timeout = 10 [(validate.rules).duration = {\\n171:     lte {seconds: 3600}\\n172:     gte {}\\n173:   }];\\n174: \\n175:   // Prevents clearing the route-cache when the\\n176:   // :ref:`clear_route_cache <envoy_v3_api_field_service.ext_proc.v3.CommonResponse.clear_route_cache>`\\n177:   // field is set in an external processor response.\\n178:   bool disable_clear_route_cache = 11;\\n179: \\n180:   // Allow headers matching the ``forward_rules`` to be forwarded to the external processing server.\\n181:   // If not set, all headers are forwarded to the external processing server.\\n182:   HeaderForwardingRules forward_rules = 12;\\n183: \\n184:   // Additional metadata to be added to the filter state for logging purposes. The metadata\\n185:   // will be added to StreamInfo's filter state under the namespace corresponding to the\\n186:   // ext_proc filter name.\\n187:   google.protobuf.Struct filter_metadata = 13;\\n188: \\n189:   // If ``allow_mode_override`` is set to true, the filter config :ref:`processing_mode\\n190:   // <envoy_v3_api_field_extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor.processing_mode>`\\n191:   // can be overridden by the response message from the external processing server\\n192:   // :ref:`mode_override <envoy_v3_api_field_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingResponse.mode_override>`.\\n193:   // If not set, ``mode_override`` API in the response message will be ignored.\\n194:   bool allow_mode_override = 14;\\n195: \\n196:   // If set to true, ignore the\\n197:   // :ref:`immediate_response <envoy_v3_api_field_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingResponse.immediate_response>`\\n198:   // message in an external processor response. In such case, no local reply will be sent.\\n199:   // Instead, the stream to the external processor will be closed. There will be no\\n200:   // more external processing for this stream from now on.\\n201:   bool disable_immediate_response = 15;\\n202: \\n203:   // Options related to the sending and receiving of dynamic metadata.\\n204:   MetadataOptions metadata_options = 16;\\n205: \\n206:   // If true, send each part of the HTTP request or response specified by ProcessingMode\\n207:   // without pausing on filter chain iteration. It is \\\"Send and Go\\\" mode that can be used\\n208:   // by external processor to observe Envoy data and status. In this mode:\\n209:   //\\n210:   // 1. Only STREAMED body processing mode is supported and any other body processing modes will be\\n211:   // ignored. NONE mode(i.e., skip body processing) will still work as expected.\\n212:   //\\n213:   // 2. External processor should not send back processing response, as any responses will be ignored.\\n214:   // This also means that\\n215:   // :ref:`message_timeout <envoy_v3_api_field_extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor.message_timeout>`\\n216:   // restriction doesn't apply to this mode.\\n217:   //\\n218:   // 3. External processor may still close the stream to indicate that no more messages are needed.\\n219:   //\\n220:   // .. warning::\\n221:   //\\n222:   //    Flow control is necessary mechanism to prevent the fast sender (either downstream client or upstream server)\\n223:   //    from overwhelming the external processor when its processing speed is slower.\\n224:   //    This protective measure is being explored and developed but has not been ready yet, so please use your own\\n225:   //    discretion when enabling this feature.\\n226:   //    This work is currently tracked under https://github.com/envoyproxy/envoy/issues/33319.\\n227:   //\\n228:   bool observability_mode = 17;\\n229: }\\n230: \\n231: // The MetadataOptions structure defines options for the sending and receiving of\\n232: // dynamic metadata. Specifically, which namespaces to send to the server, whether\\n233: // metadata returned by the server may be written, and how that metadata may be written.\\n234: message MetadataOptions {\\n235:   message MetadataNamespaces {\\n236:     // Specifies a list of metadata namespaces whose values, if present,\\n237:     // will be passed to the ext_proc service as an opaque *protobuf::Struct*.\\n238:     repeated string untyped = 1;\\n239: \\n240:     // Specifies a list of metadata namespaces whose values, if present,\\n241:     // will be passed to the ext_proc service as a *protobuf::Any*. This allows\\n242:     // envoy and the external processing server to share the protobuf message\\n243:     // definition for safe parsing.\\n244:     repeated string typed = 2;\\n245:   }\\n246: \\n247:   // Describes which typed or untyped dynamic metadata namespaces to forward to\\n248:   // the external processing server.\\n249:   MetadataNamespaces forwarding_namespaces = 1;\\n250: \\n251:   // Describes which typed or untyped dynamic metadata namespaces to accept from\\n252:   // the external processing server. Set to empty or leave unset to disallow writing\\n253:   // any received dynamic metadata. Receiving of typed metadata is not supported.\\n254:   MetadataNamespaces receiving_namespaces = 2;\\n255: }\\n256: \\n257: // The HeaderForwardingRules structure specifies what headers are\\n258: // allowed to be forwarded to the external processing server.\\n259: //\\n260: // This works as below:\\n261: //\\n262: //   1. If neither ``allowed_headers`` nor ``disallowed_headers`` is set, all headers are forwarded.\\n263: //   2. If both ``allowed_headers`` and ``disallowed_headers`` are set, only headers in the\\n264: //      ``allowed_headers`` but not in the ``disallowed_headers`` are forwarded.\\n265: //   3. If ``allowed_headers`` is set, and ``disallowed_headers`` is not set, only headers in\\n266: //      the ``allowed_headers`` are forwarded.\\n267: //   4. If ``disallowed_headers`` is set, and ``allowed_headers`` is not set, all headers except\\n268: //      headers in the ``disallowed_headers`` are forwarded.\\n269: message HeaderForwardingRules {\\n270:   // If set, specifically allow any header in this list to be forwarded to the external\\n271:   // processing server. This can be overridden by the below ``disallowed_headers``.\\n272:   type.matcher.v3.ListStringMatcher allowed_headers = 1;\\n273: \\n274:   // If set, specifically disallow any header in this list to be forwarded to the external\\n275:   // processing server. This overrides the above ``allowed_headers`` if a header matches both.\\n276:   type.matcher.v3.ListStringMatcher disallowed_headers = 2;\\n277: }\\n278: \\n279: // Extra settings that may be added to per-route configuration for a\\n280: // virtual host or cluster.\\n281: message ExtProcPerRoute {\\n282:   oneof override {\\n283:     option (validate.required) = true;\\n284: \\n285:     // Disable the filter for this particular vhost or route.\\n286:     // If disabled is specified in multiple per-filter-configs, the most specific one will be used.\\n287:     bool disabled = 1 [(validate.rules).bool = {const: true}];\\n288: \\n289:     // Override aspects of the configuration for this route. A set of\\n290:     // overrides in a more specific configuration will override a \\\"disabled\\\"\\n291:     // flag set in a less-specific one.\\n292:     ExtProcOverrides overrides = 2;\\n293:   }\\n294: }\\n295: \\n296: // Overrides that may be set on a per-route basis\\n297: // [#next-free-field: 8]\\n298: message ExtProcOverrides {\\n299:   // Set a different processing mode for this route than the default.\\n300:   ProcessingMode processing_mode = 1;\\n301: \\n302:   // [#not-implemented-hide:]\\n303:   // Set a different asynchronous processing option than the default.\\n304:   bool async_mode = 2;\\n305: \\n306:   // [#not-implemented-hide:]\\n307:   // Set different optional attributes than the default setting of the\\n308:   // ``request_attributes`` field.\\n309:   repeated string request_attributes = 3;\\n310: \\n311:   // [#not-implemented-hide:]\\n312:   // Set different optional properties than the default setting of the\\n313:   // ``response_attributes`` field.\\n314:   repeated string response_attributes = 4;\\n315: \\n316:   // Set a different gRPC service for this route than the default.\\n317:   config.core.v3.GrpcService grpc_service = 5;\\n318: \\n319:   // Options related to the sending and receiving of dynamic metadata.\\n320:   // Lists of forwarding and receiving namespaces will be overridden in their entirety,\\n321:   // meaning the most-specific config that specifies this override will be the final\\n322:   // config used. It is the prerogative of the control plane to ensure this\\n323:   // most-specific config contains the correct final overrides.\\n324:   MetadataOptions metadata_options = 6;\\n325: \\n326:   // Additional metadata to include into streams initiated to the ext_proc gRPC\\n327:   // service. This can be used for scenarios in which additional ad hoc\\n328:   // authorization headers (e.g. ``x-foo-bar: baz-key``) are to be injected or\\n329:   // when a route needs to partially override inherited metadata.\\n330:   repeated config.core.v3.HeaderValue grpc_initial_metadata = 7;\\n331: }\\n332: syntax = \\\"proto3\\\";\\n2: \\n3: package envoy.extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3;\\n4: \\n5: import \\\"envoy/config/common/mutation_rules/v3/mutation_rules.proto\\\";\\n6: import \\\"envoy/config/core/v3/base.proto\\\";\\n7: import \\\"envoy/config/core/v3/grpc_service.proto\\\";\\n8: import \\\"envoy/extensions/filters/http/ext_proc/v3/processing_mode.proto\\\";\\n9: import [#protodoc-title: External Processing Filter]\\n24: // External Processing Filter\\n25: // [#extension: envoy.filters.http.ext_proc]\\n26: \\n27: // The External Processing filter allows an external service to act on HTTP traffic in a flexible way.\\n28: \\n29: // **Current Implementation Status:**\\n30: // All options and processing modes are implemented except for the following:\\n31: //\\n32: // * \\\"async mode\\\" is not implemented.\\n33: \\n34: // The filter communicates with an external gRPC service called an \\\"external processor\\\"\\n35: // that can do a variety of things with the request and response:\\n36: //\\n37: // * Access and modify the HTTP headers on the request, response, or both\\n38: // * Access and modify the HTTP request and response bodies\\n39: // * Access and modify the dynamic stream metadata\\n40: // * Immediately send an HTTP response downstream and terminate other processing\\n41: //\\n42: // The filter communicates with the server using a gRPC bidirectional stream. After the initial\\n43: // request, the external server is in control over what additional data is sent to it\\n44: // and how it should be processed.\\n45: //\\n46: // By implementing the protocol specified by the stream, the external server can choose:\\n47: //\\n48: // * Whether it receives the response message at all\\n49: // * Whether it receives the message body at all, in separate chunks, or as a single buffer\\n50: // * Whether subsequent HTTP requests are transmitted synchronously or whether they are\\n51: //   sent asynchronously.\\n52: // * To modify request or response trailers if they already exist\\n53: //\\n54: // The filter supports up to six different processing steps. Each is represented by\\n55: // a gRPC stream message that is sent to the external processor. For each message, the\\n56: // processor must send a matching response.\\n57: //\\n58: // * Request headers: Contains the headers from the original HTTP request.\\n59: // * Request body: Delivered if they are present and sent in a single message if\\n60: //   the BUFFERED or BUFFERED_PARTIAL mode is chosen, in multiple messages if the\\n61: //   STREAMED mode is chosen, and not at all otherwise.\\n62: // * Request trailers: Delivered if they are present and if the trailer mode is set\\n63: //   to SEND.\\n64: // * Response headers: Contains the headers from the HTTP response. Keep in mind\\n65: //   that if the upstream system sends them before processing the request body that\\n66: //   this message may arrive before the complete body.\\n67: // * Response body: Sent according to the processing mode like the request body.\\n68: // * Response trailers: Delivered according to the processing mode like the\\n69: //   request trailers.\\n70: //\\n71: // By default, the processor sends only the request and response headers messages.\\n72: // This may be changed to include any of the six steps by changing the processing_mode\\n73: // setting of the filter configuration, or by setting the mode_override of any response\\n74: // from the external processor. The latter is only enabled if allow_mode_override is\\n75: // set to true. This way, a processor may, for example, use information\\n76: // in the request header to determine whether the message body must be examined, or whether\\n77: // the proxy should simply stream it straight through.\\n78: //\\n79: // All of this together allows a server to process the filter traffic in fairly\\n80: // sophisticated ways. For example:\\n81: //\\n82: // * A server may choose to examine all or part of the HTTP message bodies depending\\n83: //   on the content of the headers.\\n84: // * A server may choose to immediately reject some messages based on their HTTP\\n85: //   headers (or other dynamic metadata) and more carefully examine others.\\n86: // * A server may asynchronously monitor traffic coming through the filter by inspecting\\n87: //   headers, bodies, or both, and then decide to switch to a synchronous processing\\n88: //   mode, either permanently or temporarily.\\n89: //\\n90: // The protocol itself is based on a bidirectional gRPC stream. Envoy will send the\\n91: // server\\n92: // :ref:`ProcessingRequest <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingRequest>`\\n93: // messages, and the server must reply with\\n94: // :ref:`ProcessingResponse <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingResponse>`.\\n95: //\\n96: // Stats about each gRPC call are recorded in a :ref:`dynamic filter state\\n97: // <arch_overview_advanced_filter_state_sharing>` object in a namespace matching the filter\\n98: // name.\\n99: //\\n100: // [#next-free-field: 18]\\n101: message ExternalProcessor {\\n102:   reserved 4;\\n103: \\n104:   reserved \\\"async_mode\\\";\\n105: \\n106:   // Configuration for the gRPC service that the filter will communicate with.\\n107:   // The filter supports both the \\\"Envoy\\\" and \\\"Google\\\" gRPC clients.\\n108:   config.core.v3.GrpcService grpc_service = 1 [(validate.rules).message = {required: true}];\\n109: \\n110:   // By default, if the gRPC stream cannot be established, or if it is closed\\n111:   // prematurely with an error, the filter will fail. Specifically, if the\\n112:   // response headers have not yet been delivered, then it will return a 500\\n113:   // error downstream. If they have been delivered, then instead the HTTP stream to the\\n114:   // downstream client will be reset.\\n115:   // With this parameter set to true, however, then if the gRPC stream is prematurely closed\\n116:   // or could not be opened, processing continues without error.\\n117:   bool failure_mode_allow = 2;\\n118: \\n119:   // Specifies default options for how HTTP headers, trailers, and bodies are\\n120:   // sent. See ProcessingMode for details.\\n121:   ProcessingMode processing_mode = 3;\\n122: \\n123:   // Envoy provides a number of :ref:`attributes <arch_overview_attributes>`\\n124:   // for expressive policies. Each attribute name provided in this field will be\\n125:   // matched against that list and populated in the request_headers message.\\n126:   // See the :ref:`attribute documentation <arch_overview_request_attributes>`\\n127:   // for the list of supported attributes and their types.\\n128:   repeated string request_attributes = 5;\\n129: \\n130:   // Envoy provides a number of :ref:`attributes <arch_overview_attributes>`\\n131:   // for expressive policies. Each attribute name provided in this field will be\\n132:   // matched against that list and populated in the response_headers message.\\n133:   // See the :ref:`attribute documentation <arch_overview_attributes>`\\n134:   // for the list of supported attributes and their types.\\n135:   repeated string response_attributes = 6;\\n136: \\n137:   // Specifies the timeout for each individual message sent on the stream and\\n138:   // when the filter is running in synchronous mode. Whenever the proxy sends\\n139:   // a message on the stream that requires a response, it will reset this timer,\\n140:   // and will stop processing and return an error (subject to the processing mode)\\n141:   // if the timer expires before a matching response is received. There is no\\n142:   // timeout when the filter is running in asynchronous mode. Zero is a valid\\n143:   // config which means the timer will be triggered immediately. If not\\n144:   // configured, default is 200 milliseconds.\\n145:   google.protobuf.Duration message_timeout = 7 [(validate.rules).duration = {\\n146:     lte {seconds: 3600}\\n147:     gte {}\\n148:   }];\\n149: \\n150:   // Optional additional prefix to use when emitting statistics. This allows to distinguish\\n151:   // emitted statistics between configured *ext_proc* filters in an HTTP filter chain.\\n152:   string stat_prefix = 8;\\n153: \\n154:   // Rules that determine what modifications an external processing server may\\n155:   // make to message headers. If not set, all headers may be modified except\\n156:   // for \\\"host\\\", \\\":authority\\\", \\\":scheme\\\", \\\":method\\\", and headers that start\\n157:   // with the header prefix set via\\n158:   // :ref:`header_prefix <envoy_v3_api_field_config.bootstrap.v3.Bootstrap.header_prefix>`\\n159:   // (which is usually \\\"x-envoy\\\").\\n160:   // Note that changing headers such as \\\"host\\\" or \\\":authority\\\" may not in itself\\n161:   // change Envoy's routing decision, as routes can be cached. To also force the\\n162:   // route to be recomputed, set the\\n163:   // :ref:`clear_route_cache <envoy_v3_api_field_service.ext_proc.v3.CommonResponse.clear_route_cache>`\\n164:   // field to true in the same response.\\n165:   config.common.mutation_rules.v3.HeaderMutationRules mutation_rules = 9;\\n166: \\n167:   // Specify the upper bound of\\n168:   // :ref:`override_message_timeout <envoy_v3_api_field_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingResponse.override_message_timeout>`\\n169:   // If not specified, by default it is 0, which will effectively disable the ``override_message_timeout`` API.\\n170:   google.protobuf.Duration max_message_timeout = 10 [(validate.rules).duration = {\\n171:     lte {seconds: 3600}\\n172:     gte {}\\n173:   }];\\n174: \\n175:   // Prevents clearing the route-cache when the\\n176:   // :ref:`clear_route_cache <envoy_v3_api_field_service.ext_proc.v3.CommonResponse.clear_route_cache>`\\n177:   // field is set in an external processor response.\\n178:   bool disable_clear_route_cache = 11;\\n179: \\n180:   // Allow headers matching the ``forward_rules`` to be forwarded to the external processing server.\\n181:   // If not set, all headers are forwarded to the external processing server.\\n182:   HeaderForwardingRules forward_rules = 12;\\n183: \\n184:   // Additional metadata to be added to the filter state for logging purposes. The metadata\\n185:   // will be added to StreamInfo's filter state under the namespace corresponding to the\\n186:   // ext_proc filter name.\\n187:   google.protobuf.Struct filter_metadata = 13;\\n188: \\n189:   // If ``allow_mode_override`` is set to true, the filter config :ref:`processing_mode\\n190:   // <envoy_v3_api_field_extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor.processing_mode>`\\n191:   // can be overridden by the response message from the external processing server\\n192:   // :ref:`mode_override <envoy_v3_api_field_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingResponse.mode_override>`.\\n193:   // If not set, ``mode_override`` API in the response message will be ignored.\\n194:   bool allow_mode_override = 14;\\n195: \\n196:   // If set to true, ignore the\\n197:   // :ref:`immediate_response <envoy_v3_api_field_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingResponse.immediate_response>`\\n198:   // message in an external processor response. In such case, no local reply will be sent.\\n199:   // Instead, the stream to the external processor will be closed. There will be no\\n200:   // more external processing for this stream from now on.\\n201:   bool disable_immediate_response = 15;\\n202: \\n203:   // Options related to the sending and receiving of dynamic metadata.\\n204:   MetadataOptions metadata_options = 16;\\n205: \\n206:   // If true, send each part of the HTTP request or response specified by ProcessingMode\\n207:   // without pausing on filter chain iteration. It is \\\"Send and Go\\\" mode that can be used\\n208:   // by external processor to observe Envoy data and status. In this mode:\\n209:   //\\n210:   // 1. Only STREAMED body processing mode is supported and any other body processing modes will be\\n211:   // ignored. NONE mode(i.e., skip body processing) will still work as expected.\\n212:   //\\n213:   // 2. External processor should not send back processing response, as any responses will be ignored.\\n214:   // This also means that\\n215:   // :ref:`message_timeout <envoy_v3_api_field_extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor.message_timeout>`\\n216:   // restriction doesn't apply to this mode.\\n217:   //\\n218:   // 3. External processor may still close the stream to indicate that no more messages are needed.\\n219:   //\\n220:   // .. warning::\\n221:   //\\n222:   //    Flow control is necessary mechanism to prevent the fast sender (either downstream client or upstream server)\\n223:   //    from overwhelming the external processor when its processing speed is slower.\\n224:   //    This protective measure is being explored and developed but has not been ready yet, so please use your own\\n225:   //    discretion when enabling this feature.\\n226:   //    This work is currently tracked under https://github.com/envoyproxy/envoy/issues/33319.\\n227:   //\\n228:   bool observability_mode = 17;\\n229: }\\n230: \\n231: // The MetadataOptions structure defines options for the sending and receiving of\\n232: // dynamic metadata. Specifically, which namespaces to send to the server, whether\\n233: // metadata returned by the server may be written, and how that metadata may be written.\\n234: message MetadataOptions {\\n235:   message MetadataNamespaces {\\n236:     // Specifies a list of metadata namespaces whose values, if present,\\n237:     // will be passed to the ext_proc service as an opaque *protobuf::Struct*.\\n238:     repeated string untyped = 1;\\n239: \\n240:     // Specifies a list of metadata namespaces whose values, if present,\\n241:     // will be passed to the ext_proc service as a *protobuf::Any*. This allows\\n242:     // envoy and the external processing server to share the protobuf message\\n243:     // definition for safe parsing.\\n244:     repeated string typed = 2;\\n245:   }\\n246: \\n247:   // Describes which typed or untyped dynamic metadata namespaces to forward to\\n248:   // the external processing server.\\n249:   MetadataNamespaces forwarding_namespaces = 1;\\n250: \\n251:   // Describes which typed or untyped dynamic metadata namespaces to accept from\\n252:   // the external processing server. Set to empty or leave unset to disallow writing\\n253:   // any received dynamic metadata. Receiving of typed metadata is not supported.\\n254:   MetadataNamespaces receiving_namespaces = 2;\\n255: }\\n256: \\n257: // The HeaderForwardingRules structure specifies what headers are\\n258: // allowed to be forwarded to the external processing server.\\n259: //\\n260: // This works as below:\\n261: //\\n262: //   1. If neither ``allowed_headers`` nor ``disallowed_headers`` is set, all headers are forwarded.\\n263: //   2. If both ``allowed_headers`` and ``disallowed_headers`` are set, only headers in the\\n264: //      ``allowed_headers`` but not in the ``disallowed_headers`` are forwarded.\\n265: //   3. {"type":"user","message":{"role":"user","content":[{"tool_use_id":"toolu_01GbfAZBpyXVeLXj1iM4aedZ","type":"tool_result","content":"{\"content\":\"1: syntax = \\\"proto3\\\";\\n2: \\n3: package java_outer_classname = \\\"ExtProcProto\\\";\\n20: option java_multiple_files = true;\\n21: option go_package = \\\"github.com/envoyproxy/go-control-plane/envoy/extensions/filters/http/ext_proc/v3;ext_procv3\\\";\\n22: option (udpa.annotations.file_status).package_version_status = ACTIVE;\\n23: \\n24: // [#protodoc-title: External Processing Filter]\\n25: // External Processing Filter\\n26: // [#extension: envoy.filters.http.ext_proc]\\n27: \\n28: // The External Processing filter allows an external service to act on HTTP traffic in a flexible way.\\n29: \\n30: // **Current Implementation Status:**\\n31: // All options and processing modes are implemented except for the following:\\n32: //\\n33: // * \\\"async mode\\\" is not implemented.\\n34: \\n35: // The filter communicates with an external gRPC service called an \\\"external processor\\\"\\n36: // that can do a variety of things with the request and response:\\n37: //\\n38: // * Access and modify the HTTP headers on the request, response, or both\\n39: // * Access and modify the HTTP request and response bodies\\n40: // * Access and modify the dynamic stream metadata\\n41: // * Immediately send an HTTP response downstream and terminate other processing\\n42: //\\n43: // The filter communicates with the server using a gRPC bidirectional stream. After the initial\\n44: // request, the external server is in control over what additional data is sent to it\\n45: // and how it should be processed.\\n46: //\\n47: // By implementing the protocol specified by the stream, the external server can choose:\\n48: //\\n49: // * Whether it receives the response message at all\\n50: // * Whether it receives the message body at all, in separate chunks, or as a single buffer\\n51: // * Whether subsequent HTTP requests are transmitted synchronously or whether they are\\n52: //   sent asynchronously.\\n53: // * To modify request or response trailers if they already exist\\n54: //\\n55: // The filter supports up to six different processing steps. Each is represented by\\n56: // a gRPC stream message that is sent to the external processor. For each message, the\\n57: // processor must send a matching response.\\n58: //\\n59: // * Request headers: Contains the headers from the original HTTP request.\\n60: // * Request body: Delivered if they are present and sent in a single message if\\n61: //   the BUFFERED or BUFFERED_PARTIAL mode is chosen, in multiple messages if the\\n62: //   STREAMED mode is chosen, and not at all otherwise.\\n63: // * Request trailers: Delivered if they are present and if the trailer mode is set\\n64: //   to SEND.\\n65: // * Response headers: Contains the headers from the HTTP response. Keep in mind\\n66: //   that if the upstream system sends them before processing the request body that\\n67: //   this message may arrive before the complete body.\\n68: // * Response body: Sent according to the processing mode like the request body.\\n69: // * Response trailers: Delivered according to the processing mode like the\\n70: //   request trailers.\\n71: //\\n72: // By default, the processor sends only the request and response headers messages.\\n73: // This may be changed to include any of the six steps by changing the processing_mode\\n74: // setting of the filter configuration, or by setting the mode_override of any response\\n75: // from the external processor. The latter is only enabled if allow_mode_override is\\n76: // set to true. This way, a processor may, for example, use information\\n77: // in the request header to determine whether the message body must be examined, or whether\\n78: // the proxy should simply stream it straight through.\\n79: //\\n80: // All of this together allows a server to process the filter traffic in fairly\\n81: // sophisticated ways. For example:\\n82: //\\n83: // * A server may choose to examine all or part of the HTTP message bodies depending\\n84: //   on the content of the headers.\\n85: // * A server may choose to immediately reject some messages based on their HTTP\\n86: //   headers (or other dynamic metadata) and more carefully examine others.\\n87: // * A server may asynchronously monitor traffic coming through the filter by inspecting\\n88: //   headers, bodies, or both, and then decide to switch to a synchronous processing\\n89: //   mode, either permanently or temporarily.\\n90: //\\n91: // The protocol itself is based on a bidirectional gRPC stream. Envoy will send the\\n92: // server\\n93: // :ref:`ProcessingRequest <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingRequest>`\\n94: // messages, and the server must reply with\\n95: // :ref:`ProcessingResponse <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingResponse>`.\\n96: //\\n97: // Stats about each gRPC call are recorded in a :ref:`dynamic filter state\\n98: // <arch_overview_advanced_filter_state_sharing>` object in a namespace matching the filter\\n99: // name.\\n100: //\\n101: // [#next-free-field: 20]\\n102: message ExternalProcessor {\\n103:   // Describes the route cache action to be taken when an external processor response\\n104:   // is received in response to request headers.\\n105:   enum RouteCacheAction {\\n106:     // The default behavior is to clear the route cache only when the\\n107:     // :ref:`clear_route_cache <envoy_v3_api_field_service.ext_proc.v3.CommonResponse.clear_route_cache>`\\n108:     // field is set in an external processor response.\\n109:     DEFAULT = 0;\\n110: \\n111:     // Always clear the route cache irrespective of the clear_route_cache bit in\\n112:     // the external processor response.\\n113:     CLEAR = 1;\\n114: \\n115:     // Do not clear the route cache irrespective of the clear_route_cache bit in\\n116:     // the external processor response. Setting to RETAIN is equivalent to set the\\n117:     // :ref:`disable_clear_route_cache <envoy_v3_api_field_extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor.disable_clear_route_cache>`\\n118:     // to true.\\n119:     RETAIN = 2;\\n120:   }\\n121: \\n122:   reserved 4;\\n123: \\n124:   reserved \\\"async_mode\\\";\\n125: \\n126:   // Configuration for the gRPC service that the filter will communicate with.\\n127:   // The filter supports both the \\\"Envoy\\\" and \\\"Google\\\" gRPC clients.\\n128:   config.core.v3.GrpcService grpc_service = 1 [(validate.rules).message = {required: true}];\\n129: \\n130:   // By default, if the gRPC stream cannot be established, or if it is closed\\n131:   // prematurely with an error, the filter will fail. Specifically, if the\\n132:   // response headers have not yet been delivered, then it will return a 500\\n133:   // error downstream. If they have been delivered, then instead the HTTP stream to the\\n134:   // downstream client will be reset.\\n135:   // With this parameter set to true, however, then if the gRPC stream is prematurely closed\\n136:   // or could not be opened, processing continues without error.\\n137:   bool failure_mode_allow = 2;\\n138: \\n139:   // Specifies default options for how HTTP headers, trailers, and bodies are\\n140:   // sent. syntax = \\\"proto3\\\";\\n2: \\n3: package envoy.extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3;\\n4: \\n5: import \\\"envoy/config/common/mutation_rules/v3/mutation_rules.proto\\\";\\n6: import \\\"envoy/config/core/v3/base.proto\\\";\\n7: import \\\"envoy/config/core/v3/grpc_service.proto\\\";\\n8: import \\\"envoy/extensions/filters/http/ext_proc/v3/processing_mode.proto\\\";\\n9: import \\\"envoy/type/matcher/v3/string.proto\\\";\\n10: \\n11: import \\\"google/protobuf/duration.proto\\\";\\n12: import \\\"google/protobuf/struct.proto\\\";\\n13: \\n14: import \\\"udpa/annotations/migrate.proto\\\";\\n15: import \\\"udpa/annotations/status.proto\\\";\\n16: import \\\"validate/validate.proto\\\";\\n17: \\n18: option java_package = \\\"io.envoyproxy.envoy.extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3\\\";\\n19: option java_outer_classname = \\\"ExtProcProto\\\";\\n20: option java_multiple_files = true;\\n21: option go_package = \\\"github.com/envoyproxy/go-control-plane/envoy/extensions/filters/http/ext_proc/v3;ext_procv3\\\";\\n22: option (udpa.annotations.file_status).package_version_status = ACTIVE;\\n23: \\n24: // [#protodoc-title: External Processing Filter]\\n25: // External Processing Filter\\n26: // [#extension: envoy.filters.http.ext_proc]\\n27: \\n28: // The External Processing filter allows an external service to act on HTTP traffic in a flexible way.\\n29: \\n30: // **Current Implementation Status:**\\n31: // All options and processing modes are implemented except for the following:\\n32: //\\n33: // * \\\"async mode\\\" is not implemented.\\n34: \\n35: // The filter communicates with an external gRPC service called an \\\"external processor\\\"\\n36: // that can do a variety of things with the request and response:\\n37: //\\n38: // * Access and modify the HTTP headers on the request, response, or both\\n39: // * Access and modify the HTTP request and response bodies\\n40: // * Access and modify the dynamic stream metadata\\n41: // * Immediately send an HTTP response downstream and terminate other processing\\n42: //\\n43: // The filter communicates with the server using a gRPC bidirectional stream. After the initial\\n44: // request, the external server is in control over what additional data is sent to it\\n45: // and how it should be processed.\\n46: //\\n47: // By implementing the protocol specified by the stream, the external server can choose:\\n48: //\\n49: // * Whether it receives the response message at all\\n50: // * Whether it receives the message body at all, in separate chunks, or as a single buffer\\n51: // * Whether subsequent HTTP requests are transmitted synchronously or whether they are\\n52: //   sent asynchronously.\\n53: // * To modify request or response trailers if they already exist\\n54: //\\n55: // The filter supports up to six different processing steps. Each is represented by\\n56: // a gRPC stream message that is sent to the external processor. For each message, the\\n57: // processor must send a matching response.\\n58: //\\n59: // * Request headers: Contains the headers from the original HTTP request.\\n60: // * Request body: Delivered if they are present and sent in a single message if\\n61: //   the BUFFERED or BUFFERED_PARTIAL mode is chosen, in multiple messages if the\\n62: //   STREAMED mode is chosen, and not at all otherwise.\\n63: // * Request trailers: Delivered if they are present and if the trailer mode is set\\n64: //   to SEND.\\n65: // * Response headers: Contains the headers from the HTTP response. Keep in mind\\n66: //   that if the upstream system sends them before processing the request body that\\n67: //   this message may arrive before the complete body.\\n68: // * Response body: Sent according to the processing mode like the request body.\\n69: // * Response trailers: Delivered according to the processing mode like the\\n70: //   request trailers.\\n71: //\\n72: // By default, the processor sends only the request and response headers messages.\\n73: // This may be changed to include any of the six steps by changing the processing_mode\\n74: // setting of the filter configuration, or by setting the mode_override of any response\\n75: // from the external processor. The latter is only enabled if allow_mode_override is\\n76: // set to true. This way, a processor may, for example, use information\\n77: // in the request header to determine whether the message body must be examined, or whether\\n78: // the proxy should simply stream it straight through.\\n79: //\\n80: // All of this together allows a server to process the filter traffic in fairly\\n81: // sophisticated ways. For example:\\n82: //\\n83: // * A server may choose to examine all or part of the HTTP message bodies depending\\n84: //   on the content of the headers.\\n85: // * A server may choose to immediately reject some messages based on their HTTP\\n86: //   headers (or other dynamic metadata) and more carefully examine others.\\n87: // * A server may asynchronously monitor traffic coming through the filter by inspecting\\n88: //   headers, bodies, or both, and then decide to switch to a synchronous processing\\n89: //   mode, either permanently or temporarily.\\n90: //\\n91: // The protocol itself is based on a bidirectional gRPC stream. Envoy will send the\\n92: // server\\n93: // :ref:`ProcessingRequest <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingRequest>`\\n94: // messages, and the server must reply with\\n95: // :ref:`ProcessingResponse <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingResponse>`.\\n96: //\\n97: // Stats about each gRPC call are recorded in a :ref:`dynamic filter state\\n98: // <arch_overview_advanced_filter_state_sharing>` object in a namespace matching the filter\\n99: // name.\\n100: //\\n101: // [#next-free-field: 20]\\n102: message ExternalProcessor {\\n103:   // Describes the route cache action to be taken when an external processor response\\n104:   // is received in response to request headers.\\n105:   enum RouteCacheAction {\\n106:     // The default behavior is to clear the route cache only when the\\n107:     // :ref:`clear_route_cache <envoy_v3_api_field_service.ext_proc.v3.CommonResponse.clear_route_cache>`\\n108:     // field is set in an external processor response.\\n109:     DEFAULT = 0;\\n110: \\n111:     // Always clear the route cache irrespective of the clear_route_cache bit in\\n112:     // the external processor response.\\n113:     CLEAR = 1;\\n114: \\n115:     // Do not clear the route cache irrespective of the clear_route_cache bit in\\n116:     // the external processor response. Setting to RETAIN is equivalent to set the\\n117:     // :ref:`disable_clear_route_cache <envoy_v3_api_field_extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor.disable_clear_route_cache>`\\n118:     // to true.\\n119:     RETAIN = 2;\\n120:   }\\n121: \\n122:   reserved 4;\\n123: \\n124:   reserved \\\"async_mode\\\";\\n125: \\n126:   // Configuration for the gRPC service that the filter will communicate with.\\n127:   // The filter supports both the \\\"Envoy\\\" and \\\"Google\\\" gRPC clients.\\n128:   config.core.v3.GrpcService grpc_service = 1 [(validate.rules).message = {required: true}];\\n129: \\n130:   // By default, if the gRPC stream cannot be established, or if it is closed\\n131:   // prematurely with an error, the filter will fail. Specifically, if the\\n132:   // response headers have not yet been delivered, then it will return a 500\\n133:   // error downstream. If they have been delivered, then instead the HTTP stream to the\\n134:   // downstream client will be reset.\\n135:   // With this parameter set to true, however, then if the gRPC stream is prematurely closed\\n136:   // or could not be opened, processing continues without error.\\n137:   bool failure_mode_allow = 2;\\n138: \\n139:   // Specifies default options for how HTTP headers, trailers, and bodies are\\n140:   // sent. java_outer_classname = \"ExtProcProto\";\n20: option java_multiple_files = true;\n21: option go_package = \"github.com/envoyproxy/go-control-plane/envoy/extensions/filters/http/ext_proc/v3;ext_procv3\";\n22: option (udpa.annotations.file_status).package_version_status = ACTIVE;\n23: \n24: // [#protodoc-title: External Processing Filter]\n25: // External Processing Filter\n26: // [#extension: envoy.filters.http.ext_proc]\n27: \n28: // The External Processing filter allows an external service to act on HTTP traffic in a flexible way.\n29: \n30: // **Current Implementation Status:**\n31: // All options and processing modes are implemented except for the following:\n32: //\n33: // * \"async mode\" is not implemented.\n34: \n35: // The filter communicates with an external gRPC service called an \"external processor\"\n36: // that can do a variety of things with the request and response:\n37: //\n38: // * Access and modify the HTTP headers on the request, response, or both\n39: // * Access and modify the HTTP request and response bodies\n40: // * Access and modify the dynamic stream metadata\n41: // * Immediately send an HTTP response downstream and terminate other processing\n42: //\n43: // The filter communicates with the server using a gRPC bidirectional stream. After the initial\n44: // request, the external server is in control over what additional data is sent to it\n45: // and how it should be processed.\n46: //\n47: // By implementing the protocol specified by the stream, the external server can choose:\n48: //\n49: // * Whether it receives the response message at all\n50: // * Whether it receives the message body at all, in separate chunks, or as a single buffer\n51: // * Whether subsequent HTTP requests are transmitted synchronously or whether they are\n52: //   sent asynchronously.\n53: // * To modify request or response trailers if they already exist\n54: //\n55: // The filter supports up to six different processing steps. Each is represented by\n56: // a gRPC stream message that is sent to the external processor. For each message, the\n57: // processor must send a matching response.\n58: //\n59: // * Request headers: Contains the headers from the original HTTP request.\n60: // * Request body: Delivered if they are present and sent in a single message if\n61: //   the BUFFERED or BUFFERED_PARTIAL mode is chosen, in multiple messages if the\n62: //   STREAMED mode is chosen, and not at all otherwise.\n63: // * Request trailers: Delivered if they are present and if the trailer mode is set\n64: //   to SEND.\n65: // * Response headers: Contains the headers from the HTTP response. Keep in mind\n66: //   that if the upstream system sends them before processing the request body that\n67: //   this message may arrive before the complete body.\n68: // * Response body: Sent according to the processing mode like the request body.\n69: // * Response trailers: Delivered according to the processing mode like the\n70: //   request trailers.\n71: //\n72: // By default, the processor sends only the request and response headers messages.\n73: // This may be changed to include any of the six steps by changing the processing_mode\n74: // setting of the filter configuration, or by setting the mode_override of any response\n75: // from the external processor. The latter is only enabled if allow_mode_override is\n76: // set to true. This way, a processor may, for example, use information\n77: // in the request header to determine whether the message body must be examined, or whether\n78: // the proxy should simply stream it straight through.\n79: //\n80: // All of this together allows a server to process the filter traffic in fairly\n81: // sophisticated ways. For example:\n82: //\n83: // * A server may choose to examine all or part of the HTTP message bodies depending\n84: //   on the content of the headers.\n85: // * A server may choose to immediately reject some messages based on their HTTP\n86: //   headers (or other dynamic metadata) and more carefully examine others.\n87: // * A server may asynchronously monitor traffic coming through the filter by inspecting\n88: //   headers, bodies, or both, and then decide to switch to a synchronous processing\n89: //   mode, either permanently or temporarily.\n90: //\n91: // The protocol itself is based on a bidirectional gRPC stream. Envoy will send the\n92: // server\n93: // :ref:`ProcessingRequest <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingRequest>`\n94: // messages, and the server must reply with\n95: // :ref:`ProcessingResponse <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingResponse>`.\n96: //\n97: // Stats about each gRPC call are recorded in a :ref:`dynamic filter state\n98: // <arch_overview_advanced_filter_state_sharing>` object in a namespace matching the filter\n99: // name.\n100: //\n101: // [#next-free-field: 20]\n102: message ExternalProcessor {\n103:   // Describes the route cache action to be taken when an external processor response\n104:   // is received in response to request headers.\n105:   enum RouteCacheAction {\n106:     // The default behavior is to clear the route cache only when the\n107:     // :ref:`clear_route_cache <envoy_v3_api_field_service.ext_proc.v3.CommonResponse.clear_route_cache>`\n108:     // field is set in an external processor response.\n109:     DEFAULT = 0;\n110: \n111:     // Always clear the route cache irrespective of the clear_route_cache bit in\n112:     // the external processor response.\n113:     CLEAR = 1;\n114: \n115:     // Do not clear the route cache irrespective of the clear_route_cache bit in\n116:     // the external processor response. Setting to RETAIN is equivalent to set the\n117:     // :ref:`disable_clear_route_cache <envoy_v3_api_field_extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor.disable_clear_route_cache>`\n118:     // to true.\n119:     RETAIN = 2;\n120:   }\n121: \n122:   reserved 4;\n123: \n124:   reserved \"async_mode\";\n125: \n126:   // Configuration for the gRPC service that the filter will communicate with.\n127:   // The filter supports both the \"Envoy\" and \"Google\" gRPC clients.\n128:   config.core.v3.GrpcService grpc_service = 1 [(validate.rules).message = {required: true}];\n129: \n130:   // By default, if the gRPC stream cannot be established, or if it is closed\n131:   // prematurely with an error, the filter will fail. Specifically, if the\n132:   // response headers have not yet been delivered, then it will return a 500\n133:   // error downstream. If they have been delivered, then instead the HTTP stream to the\n134:   // downstream client will be reset.\n135:   // With this parameter set to true, however, then if the gRPC stream is prematurely closed\n136:   // or could not be opened, processing continues without error.\n137:   bool failure_mode_allow = 2;\n138: \n139:   // Specifies default options for how HTTP headers, trailers, and bodies are\n140:   // sent. See ProcessingMode for details.\n141:   ProcessingMode processing_mode = 3;\n142: \n143:   // Envoy provides a number of :ref:`attributes <arch_overview_attributes>`\n144:   // for expressive policies. Each attribute name provided in this field will be\n145:   // matched against that list and populated in the request_headers message.\n146:   // See the :ref:`attribute documentation <arch_overview_request_attributes>`\n147:   // for the list of supported attributes and their types.\n148:   repeated string request_attributes = 5;\n149: \n150:   // Envoy provides a number of :ref:`attributes <arch_overview_attributes>`\n151:   // for expressive policies. Each attribute name provided in this field will be\n152:   // matched against that list and populated in the response_headers message.\n153:   // See the :ref:`attribute documentation <arch_overview_attributes>`\n154:   // for the list of supported attributes and their types.\n155:   repeated string response_attributes = 6;\n156: \n157:   // Specifies the timeout for each individual message sent on the stream and\n158:   // when the filter is running in synchronous mode. Whenever the proxy sends\n159:   // a message on the stream that requires a response, it will reset this timer,\n160:   // and will stop processing and return an error (subject to the processing mode)\n161:   // if the timer expires before a matching response is received. There is no\n162:   // timeout when the filter is running in asynchronous mode. Zero is a valid\n163:   // config which means the timer will be triggered immediately. If not\n164:   // configured, default is 200 milliseconds.\n165:   google.protobuf.Duration message_timeout = 7 [(validate.rules).duration = {\n166:     lte {seconds: 3600}\n167:     gte {}\n168:   }];\n169: \n170:   // Optional additional prefix to use when emitting statistics. This allows to distinguish\n171:   // emitted statistics between configured *ext_proc* filters in an HTTP filter chain.\n172:   string stat_prefix = 8;\n173: \n174:   // Rules that determine what modifications an external processing server may\n175:   // make to message headers. If not set, all headers may be modified except\n176:   // for \"host\", \":authority\", \":scheme\", \":method\", and headers that start\n177:   // with the header prefix set via\n178:   // :ref:`header_prefix <envoy_v3_api_field_config.bootstrap.v3.Bootstrap.header_prefix>`\n179:   // (which is usually \"x-envoy\").\n180:   // Note that changing headers such as \"host\" or \":authority\" may not in itself\n181:   // change Envoy's routing decision, as routes can be cached. To also force the\n182:   // route to be recomputed, set the\n183:   // :ref:`clear_route_cache <envoy_v3_api_field_service.ext_proc.v3.CommonResponse.clear_route_cache>`\n184:   // field to true in the same response.\n185:   config.common.mutation_rules.v3.HeaderMutationRules mutation_rules = 9;\n186: \n187:   // Specify the upper bound of\n188:   // :ref:`override_message_timeout <envoy_v3_api_field_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingResponse.override_message_timeout>`\n189:   // If not specified, by default it is 0, which will effectively disable the ``override_message_timeout`` API.\n190:   google.protobuf.Duration max_message_timeout = 10 [(validate.rules).duration = {\n191:     lte {seconds: 3600}\n192:     gte {}\n193:   }];\n194: \n195:   // Allow headers matching the ``forward_rules`` to be forwarded to the external processing server.\n196:   // If not set, all headers are forwarded to the external processing server.\n197:   HeaderForwardingRules forward_rules = 12;\n198: \n199:   // Additional metadata to be added to the filter state for logging purposes. The metadata\n200:   // will be added to StreamInfo's filter state under the namespace corresponding to the\n201:   // ext_proc filter name.\n202:   google.protobuf.Struct filter_metadata = 13;\n203: \n204:   // If ``allow_mode_override`` is set to true, the filter config :ref:`processing_mode\n205:   // <envoy_v3_api_field_extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor.processing_mode>`\n206:   // can be overridden by the response message from the external processing server\n207:   // :ref:`mode_override <envoy_v3_api_field_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingResponse.mode_override>`.\n208:   // If not set, ``mode_override`` API in the response message will be ignored.\n209:   bool allow_mode_override = 14;\n210: \n211:   // If set to true, ignore the\n212:   // :ref:`immediate_response <envoy_v3_api_field_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingResponse.immediate_response>`\n213:   // message in an external processor response. In such case, no local reply will be sent.\n214:   // Instead, the stream to the external processor will be closed. There will be no\n215:   // more external processing for this stream from now on.\n216:   bool disable_immediate_response = 15;\n217: \n218:   // Options related to the sending and receiving of dynamic metadata.\n219:   MetadataOptions metadata_options = 16;\n220: \n221:   // If true, send each part of the HTTP request or response specified by ProcessingMode\n222:   // without pausing on filter chain iteration. It is \"Send and Go\" mode that can be used\n223:   // by external processor to observe Envoy data and status. In this mode:\n224:   //\n225:   // 1. Only STREAMED body processing mode is supported and any other body processing modes will be\n226:   // ignored. NONE mode(i.e., skip body processing) will still work as expected.\n227:   //\n228:   // 2. External processor should not send back processing response, as any responses will be ignored.\n229:   // This also means that\n230:   // :ref:`message_timeout <envoy_v3_api_field_extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor.message_timeout>`\n231:   // restriction doesn't apply to this mode.\n232:   //\n233:   // 3. External processor may still close the stream to indicate that no more messages are needed.\n234:   //\n235:   // .. warning::\n236:   //\n237:   //    Flow control is necessary mechanism to prevent the fast sender (either downstream client or upstream server)\n238:   //    from overwhelming the external processor when its processing speed is slower.\n239:   //    This protective measure is being explored and developed but has not been ready yet, so please use your own\n240:   //    discretion when enabling this feature.\n241:   //    This work is currently tracked under https://github.com/envoyproxy/envoy/issues/33319.\n242:   //\n243:   bool observability_mode = 17;\n244: \n245:   // Prevents clearing the route-cache when the\n246:   // :ref:`clear_route_cache <envoy_v3_api_field_service.ext_proc.v3.CommonResponse.clear_route_cache>`\n247:   // field is set in an external processor response.\n248:   // Only one of ``disable_clear_route_cache`` or ``route_cache_action`` can be set.\n249:   // It is recommended to set ``route_cache_action`` which supersedes ``disable_clear_route_cache``.\n250:   bool disable_clear_route_cache = 11\n251:       [(udpa.annotations.field_migrate).oneof_promotion = \"clear_route_cache_type\"];\n252: \n253:   // Specifies the action to be taken when an external processor response is\n254:   // received in response to request headers. It is recommended to set this field than set\n255:   // :ref:`disable_clear_route_cache <envoy_v3_api_field_extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor.disable_clear_route_cache>`.\n256:   // Only one of ``disable_clear_route_cache`` or ``route_cache_action`` can be set.\n257:   RouteCacheAction route_cache_action = 18\n258:       [(udpa.annotations.field_migrate).oneof_promotion = \"clear_route_cache_type\"];\n259: \n260:   // Specifies the deferred closure timeout for gRPC stream that connects to external processor. Currently, the deferred stream closure\n261:   // is only used in :ref:`observability_mode <envoy_v3_api_field_extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor.observability_mode>`.\n262:   // In observability mode, gRPC streams may be held open to the external processor longer than the lifetime of the regular client to\n263:   // backend stream lifetime. In this case, Envoy will eventually timeout the external processor stream according to this time limit.\n264:   // The default value is 5000 milliseconds (5 seconds) if not specified.\n265:   google.protobuf.Duration deferred_close_timeout = 19;\n266: }\n267: \n268: // The MetadataOptions structure defines options for the sending and receiving of\n269: // dynamic metadata. Specifically, which namespaces to send to the server, whether\n270: // metadata returned by the server may be written, and how that metadata may be written.\n271: message MetadataOptions {\n272:   message MetadataNamespaces {\n273:     // Specifies a list of metadata namespaces whose values, if present,\n274:     // will be passed to the ext_proc service as an opaque *protobuf::Struct*.\n275:     repeated string untyped = 1;\n276: \n277:     // Specifies a list of metadata namespaces whose values, if present,\n278:     // will be passed to the ext_proc service as a *protobuf::Any*. Set to empty or leave unset to disallow writing\n290:   // any received dynamic metadata. Receiving of typed metadata is not supported.\n291:   MetadataNamespaces receiving_namespaces = 2;\n292: }\n293: \n294: // The HeaderForwardingRules structure specifies what headers are\n295: // allowed to be forwarded to the external processing server.\n296: //\n297: // This works as below:\n298: //\n299: //   1. If neither ``allowed_headers`` nor ``disallowed_headers`` is set, all headers are forwarded.\n300: //   2. By default, request and response headers are sent,\\n27:     // while trailers are skipped.\\n28:     DEFAULT = 0;\\n29: \\n30:     // Send the header or trailer.\\n31:     SEND = 1;\\n32: \\n33:     // Do not send the header or trailer.\\n34:     SKIP = 2;\\n35:   }\\n36: \\n37:   // Control how the request and response bodies are handled\\n38:   // When body mutation by external processor is enabled, ext_proc filter will always remove\\n39:   // the content length header in three cases below because content length can not be guaranteed\\n40:   // to be set correctly:\\n41:   // 1) STREAMED BodySendMode: header processing completes before body mutation comes back.\\n42:   // 2) BUFFERED_PARTIAL BodySendMode: body is buffered and could be injected in different phases.\\n43:   // 3) BUFFERED BodySendMode + SKIP HeaderSendMode: header processing (e.g., update content-length) is skipped.\\n44:   //\\n45:   // In Envoy's http1 codec implementation, removing content length will enable chunked transfer\\n46:   // encoding whenever feasible. The recipient (either client or server) must be able\\n47:   // to parse and decode the chunked transfer coding.\\n48:   // (see `details in RFC9112 <https://tools.ietf.org/html/rfc9112#section-7.1>`_).\\n49:   //\\n50:   // In BUFFERED BodySendMode + SEND HeaderSendMode, content length header is allowed but it is\\n51:   // external processor's responsibility to set the content length correctly matched to the length\\n52:   // of mutated body. If they don't match, the corresponding body mutation will be rejected and\\n53:   // local reply will be sent with an error message.\\n54:   enum BodySendMode {\\n55:     // Do not send the body at all. This is the default.\\n56:     NONE = 0;\\n57: \\n58:     // Stream the body to the server in pieces as they arrive at the\\n59:     // proxy.\\n60:     STREAMED = 1;\\n61: \\n62:     // Buffer the message body in memory and send the entire body at once.\\n63:     // If the body exceeds the configured buffer limit, then the\\n64:     // downstream system will receive an error.\\n65:     BUFFERED = 2;\\n66: \\n67:     // Buffer the message body in memory and send the entire body in one\\n68:     // chunk. If the body exceeds the configured buffer limit, then the body contents\\n69:     // up to the buffer limit will be sent.\\n70:     BUFFERED_PARTIAL = 3;\\n71:   }\\n72: \\n73:   // How to handle the request header. Default is \\\"SEND\\\".\\n74:   HeaderSendMode request_header_mode = 1 [(validate.rules).enum = {defined_only: true}];\\n75: \\n76:   // How to handle the response header. Default is \\\"SEND\\\".\\n77:   HeaderSendMode response_header_mode = 2 [(validate.rules).enum = {defined_only: true}];\\n78: \\n79:   // How to handle the request body. {"type":"user","message":{"role":"user","content":[{"tool_use_id":"toolu_01EQAMrKNk9UrG3pMEQ9Nhra","type":"tool_result","content":"{\"content\":\"1: .. _config_http_filters_ext_proc:\\n2: \\n3: External Processing\\n4: ===================\\n5: * This filter should be configured with the type URL ``type.googleapis.com/envoy.extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor``.\\n6: * :ref:`v3 API reference <envoy_v3_api_msg_extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor>`\\n7: \\n8: The external processing filter connects an external service, called an \\\"external processor,\\\"\\n9: to the filter chain. The processing service itself implements a gRPC interface that allows\\n10: it to respond to events in the lifecycle of an HTTP request / response by examining\\n11: and modifying the headers, body, and trailers of each message, or by returning a brand-new response.\\n12: \\n13: The protocol itself is based on a bidirectional gRPC stream. Envoy will send the\\n14: external processor\\n15: :ref:`ProcessingRequest <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingRequest>`\\n16: messages, and the processor must reply with\\n17: :ref:`ProcessingResponse <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingResponse>`\\n18: messages.\\n19: \\n20: Configuration options are provided to control which events are sent to the processor.\\n21: This way, the processor may receive headers, body, and trailers for both\\n22: request and response in any combination. The processor may also change this configuration\\n23: on a message-by-message basis. This allows for the construction of sophisticated processors\\n24: that decide how to respond to each message individually to eliminate unnecessary\\n25: stream requests from the proxy.\\n26: \\n27: This filter is a work in progress. Most of the major bits of functionality\\n28: are complete. The updated list of supported features and implementation status may\\n29: be found on the :ref:`reference page <envoy_v3_api_msg_extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor>`.\\n30: \\n31: Statistics\\n32: ----------\\n33: This filter outputs statistics in the\\n34: ``http.<stat_prefix>.ext_proc.`` namespace. The :ref:`stat prefix\\n35: <envoy_v3_api_field_extensions.filters.network.http_connection_manager.v3.HttpConnectionManager.stat_prefix>`\\n36: comes from the owning HTTP connection manager.\\n37: \\n38: The following statistics are supported:\\n39: \\n40: .. csv-table::\\n41:   :header: Name, Type, Description\\n42:   :widths: auto\\n43: \\n44:   streams_started, Counter, The number of gRPC streams that have been started to send to the external processing service\\n45:   streams_msgs_sent, Counter, The number of messages sent on those streams\\n46:   streams_msgs_received, Counter, The number of messages received on those streams\\n47:   spurious_msgs_received, Counter, The number of unexpected messages received that violated the protocol\\n48:   streams_closed, Counter, The number ``type.googleapis.com/envoy.extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor``.\n6: * :ref:`v3 API reference <envoy_v3_api_msg_extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor>`\n7: \n8: The external processing filter connects an external service, called an \"external processor,\"\n9: to the filter chain. The processing service itself implements a gRPC interface that allows\n10: it to respond to events in the lifecycle of an HTTP request / response by examining\n11: and modifying the headers, body, and trailers of each message, or by returning a brand-new response.\n12: \n13: The protocol itself is based on a bidirectional gRPC stream. Envoy will send the\n14: external processor\n15: :ref:`ProcessingRequest <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingRequest>`\n16: messages, and the processor must reply with\n17: :ref:`ProcessingResponse <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingResponse>`\n18: messages.\n19: \n20: Configuration options are provided to control which events are sent to the processor.\n21: This way, the processor may receive headers, body, and trailers for both\n22: request and response in any combination. The processor may also change this configuration\n23: on a message-by-message basis. This allows for the construction of sophisticated processors\n24: that decide how to respond to each message individually to eliminate unnecessary\n25: stream requests from the proxy.\n26: \n27: This filter is a work in progress. Most of the major bits of functionality\n28: are complete. The updated list of supported features and implementation status may\n29: be found on the :ref:`reference page <envoy_v3_api_msg_extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor>`.\n30: \n31: Statistics\n32: ----------\n33: This filter outputs statistics in the\n34: ``http.<stat_prefix>.ext_proc.`` namespace. The :ref:`stat prefix\n35: <envoy_v3_api_field_extensions.filters.network.http_connection_manager.v3.HttpConnectionManager.stat_prefix>`\n36: comes from the owning HTTP connection manager.\n37: \n38: The following statistics are supported:\n39: \n40: .. csv-table::\n41:   :header: Name, Type, Description\n42:   :widths: auto\n43: \n44:   streams_started, Counter, The number of gRPC streams that have been started to send to the external processing service\n45:   streams_msgs_sent, Counter, The number of messages sent on those streams\n46:   streams_msgs_received, Counter, The number of messages received on those streams\n47:   spurious_msgs_received, Counter, The number of unexpected messages received that violated the protocol\n48:   streams_closed, Counter, The number of streams successfully closed on either end\n49:   streams_failed, Counter, The number of times a stream produced a gRPC error\n50:   failure_mode_allowed, Counter, The number of times an error was ignored due to configuration\n51:   message_timeouts, Counter, The number of times a message failed to receive a response within the configured timeout\n52:   rejected_header_mutations, Counter, The number of rejected header mutations\n53:   clear_route_cache_ignored, Counter, The number of clear cache request that were ignored\n54:   clear_route_cache_disabled, Counter, The number of clear cache requests that were rejected from being disabled\n55: ","url":"https://sourcegraph.sourcegraph.com/github.com/sg-evals/envoy--7b8baff1@7d6a8ad71741583b3a75f94937b6f294b39e2667/-/blob/docs/root/configuration/http/http_filters/ext_proc_filter.rst"}}}

Now I have enough information to write the migration guide. Let me summarize the key changes from v1.30.0 to v1.31.0:\n\n## Key Changes in v1.31.0:\n\n### 1. **New RouteCacheAction Enum**\n   - Introduced to provide more fine-grained control over route cache clearing behavior\n   - Three values: DEFAULT, CLEAR, RETAIN\n   - RETAIN is equivalent to the old disable_clear_route_cache=true\n\n### 2. **Deprecated disable_clear_route_cache in favor of route_cache_action**\n   - The old `disable_clear_route_cache` boolean field is now deprecated\n   - New `route_cache_action` field provides three explicit options\n   - v1.31 automatically converts `disable_clear_route_cache=true` to `route_cache_action=RETAIN`\n   - Configuration validation prevents both from being set to non-default values simultaneously\n\n### 3. **New deferred_close_timeout Field**\n   - Specifies the deferred closure timeout for gRPC streams\n   - Default: 5000 milliseconds (5 seconds)\n   - Used primarily in observability_mode to control how long streams are held open\n\n### 4. **New observability_mode Field**\n   - \"Send and Go\" mode for observing traffic without expecting responses\n   - Messages are sent without waiting for processor responses\n   - Only STREAMED body mode is supported in this mode\n   - Useful for logging and monitoring without affecting latency\n   - Requires careful flow control (warning in docs)\n\n### 5. **New ThreadLocalStreamManager**\n   - Manages deferred stream closure in observability mode\n   - Implements stream lifecycle management with timeout-based cleanup\n\n### 6. **New filterMetadata Configuration**\n   - Allows adding additional metadata to filter state for logging purposes\n\nNow let me write the comprehensive migration
